## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through constitutive laws (elastic, plastic, or viscoplastic) with temperature-dependent material properties such as elastic modulus, yield stress, and hardening parameters.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain relationship)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Ramberg-Osgood type plastic hardening)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (plastic hardening with thermal softening)
- Hollomon equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening with thermal dependence)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic or rubber-like material)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon) (high-temperature deformation)
- Swift law with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (pre-strained power-law hardening with thermal effect)
- Bilinear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**2 (quadratic stress-strain with temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (1 + c*T) with negative c, or exp(-c*T) applied to stress
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 representing diminishing hardening rate (work hardening)
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) representing initial yield before hardening begins
- Temperature-modulus coupling → Product form E(T) * f(epsilon) where E(T) is a decreasing function of temperature
- Neo-Hookean/rubber elasticity → Combination of epsilon and epsilon**(-2) or similar inverse powers for hyperelastic materials
- Thermal activation of deformation → Arrhenius-like exp(-c/T) factor multiplying strain-dependent terms for thermally activated processes
- Sigmoidal stress-strain transition → tanh(c*epsilon) representing smooth elastic-to-plastic transition
